- 64 -                      ANNEX4
ANNEX 4: WATER SUPPLY METERING
1.   It is Government policy to introduce metering and to support the principle of
"user pays" pricing for all water and electricity consumers. A Government decree was
passed in 1995 that stipulates that water and electricity meters would be installed in all
individual premises by 1998. However, this involves a substantial financial commitment,
and implementation of the policy has not yet commenced. Previous studies carried out in
1994/95 under the Ministry of Energy's responsibility, have highlighted the extent of
water wastage and losses in apartment buildings, and the potential for substantial
reductions in water supply operating costs if these losses can be eliminated.
CURRENT SITUATION
2.    Ulaanbaatar's water supply network was initially equipped with water meters at
all distribution booster stations (CTP), which are located ahead of the secondary networks
serving apartment networks; all wells and pumping stations were installed without any
meter. Most of these meters have ceased functioning over time, and the water company,
USAG, has found it impossible to determine overall production rates from the wells or
amounts pumped in each of the CTPs for hot and cold water boosted to the block
buildings of the apartments.
3.    Downstream of the CTP and secondary networks, design of piping in apartments
has generally included within each stairwell two cold water rising pipes and one hot water
rising pipe. Except in the most recently constructed buildings, there is no returning hot
water pipe. All networks downstream of a CTP are currently owned and maintained by
the 17 subsidiaries of the Housing and Maintenance Service Company (OSNAAK).
These 17 subsidiaries, named kantors, are physically responsible for at least one pumping
station (CTP), a few small stocking reservoirs, the secondary networks and all plumbing
facilities in the apartment buildings.
4.    USAG remains responsible for direct water service to industries, institutional
clients such as schools and hospitals and a very limited number of domestic customers in
the center of the city. There are about 1,060 accounts directly managed by USAG.
Although 100 of these accounts are metered and have operating meters, most of the
billing has been carried out on the basis of norms established over time based on Soviet
standards and applied for both design and billing of consumers. USAG bills the CTPs on
the basis of a domestic water consumption of 150 liters per capita per day, whereas recent
water consumption surveys have demonstrated that apartment inhabitants can consume as
much as 410 lcd.
5.    The current situation of water losses in the primary distribution system owned and
maintained by USAG remains very unclear as no survey of water losses has been carried



- 65 -                     ANNEX4
out; USAG indicates that water breakages on these primary mains occur about 20 to 30
times per year. Water losses and wastage are far higher in secondary networks and
apartment plumbing fixtures. The kantors do not keep records of the number of pipe
breakages on the secondary network, but their managers state that the number of
plumbers within each kantor (one person per 1,200 to 2,000 apartments) is insufficient to
face demands caused by leaks on secondary networks, block apartment buildings and
internal apartment properties. A survey conducted in 1994 with the introduction of
experimental metering in two apartment buildings demonstrated that: (a) initially, water
consumption was at about 310 to 330 lcd; (b) after undertaking a fixture replacement
program on one building and setting individual meters on each apartment pipe riser, water
consumption dropped to about 163 lcd, while it remained at about 240 lcd without any
fixture repair program; (c) apartment inhabitants were highly conscious of the need to
conserve water by closing water taps whenever repaired, and sensitive to the introduction
of water billing based on actual consumption and had started requesting more frequent
plumbing assistance from kantor staff to maintain as low a water wastage as possible.
The survey also pointed out that the pattern of consumption also changed, with metered
apartments using much less cold water in total and percentage terms.
STRATEGY AND PROPOSALS
6.    In view of the extreme difficulty of obtaining reliable data to rationalize water
utilization and develop a satisfactory billing system, Mongolia's professional community
has recognized the need to urgently reintroduce metering and provide incentives to the
population to control the water wastage occurring either through abusive use of both hot
and cold water or leaking faucets and apartment fixtures and the deteriorating stock of
leaky pipes outside apartment properties. A first effort is under way under a preliminary
JICA-financed initiative focusing on the study and strengthening of UB's water
production assets. The JICA funding would include provision of water meters to monitor
water production by the pumping stations and installation of about 51 water meters at the
37 CTPs. This program would be completed before the end of 1997. JICA also intends
to fund the metering and automation of pumping stations of all production facilities over
the next few years.
7.    Three options for apartment metering have been considered:  (a) metering
individual apartments; (b) metering building cores (i.e., typically groups of 12 to 27
apartments); or (c) metering buildings separately (i.e., groups of more than 60
apartments). Cost estimates are, respectively, $7.7 million, $1.2 million and $0.6 million.
It is recognized that metering individual apartments may be adopted because it is most
socially equitable, and metering buildings separately is the least expensive and equitable
and would be the least likely to achieve significant water conservation. However, the
proposed option, metering building cores, is a compromise because of its acceptable cost
to the community and because it can commence the process of linking responsibility for
water consumption with the cost of water to apartment residents. It also follows logically
from the CTPs' metering and is a timely step in the process of introducing volume-based
charging.



- 66 -                     ANNEX4
8.    UB has some 755 apartment buildings with 2,618 building cores. Metering at the
stairwell level would require a total of about 3,200 metering points on the water risers; a
first survey of existing internal plumbing piping leading to the apartments shows that
there should be four meters at the base of each column to appropriately capture the
consumption of each set of stairwell residents. A more extensive survey of local
conditions is being carried out by kantors to identify the issues in developing stairwell
metering and preparing standards for equipment and installation of this major metering
undertaking.
9.    Discussions indicate agreements on the following points:
(a)   meters should be owned by USAG while being left to the responsibility of
the kantors who will be charged a maintenance fee by USAG. The repair
and maintenance of meters would be carried out at the kantors' request, by
USAG who would receive adequate testing equipment and meter spares to
carry out its maintenance role;
(b)   meter installation would be carried out by kantors' staff; the supply will
come from USAG and would include all parts to allow satisfactory
installation and potential dismantling for repair;
(c)   a first survey of typical installation conditions will be carried out in Spring
1997 to ensure good knowledge of location conditions and the nature of
parts;
(d)   the purchase of some 22,000 meters for block metering of both hot and
cold water will be included under the Credit; a first tranche of some 5,000
meters would be bid during the Year 1 implementation period, so that
installation could start by end- 1997 and extend through winter 1997-98.
10.   Trade, Industrial and Institutional Metering. USAG will resume billing of all
trade, institutional and industrial customers it used to bill according to actual
consumption. New meters would be purchased as part of the project under the first
tranche of meters supplied. As for the apartment meters, USAG would own the meters,
and would charge a rental and maintenance fee to the customer.
11.   Development of Billing Systems. The present billing system established at the
kantor level needs to be overhauled and account for the reforms introduced with the
privatization of the housing market; these new systems should also ensure that customers
can be later billed according to the quantity of water consumed. The issuance of water
supply bills by the kantors will ensure that the latter retain the responsibility and expertise
to address maintenance issues at the building block level. Kantors are also the most
appropriate unit to keep information on population and residences, and are the most
amenable to ensure appropriate collection of water bills together with other utility
charges. While ultimately through the privatization process this billing and collection
function might return to each individual utility (heating, water, power, solid wastes), the
preparation of billing systems should be devised to permit this potential change of future



- 67 -                    ANNEX4
responsibility and maintain similarity in systems across each kantor's own systems.
Similarly, USAG will need to recast it own billing system and introduce mechanisms to:
(a) obtain payment other than through bank account compensation, and (b) monitor
effective payments for the introduction of disconnection policies.
FIXTURE REPAIR PROGRAM
12.   This program aims at helping the apartment users reduce substantially the water
wastage within their apartment. The above-mentioned survey has shown that many taps
are not closing properly, many toilets are flowing constantly and occasionally internal
building piping is corroded and leaks. Under the same survey, repairs then effected
resulted in substantial water consumption reduction in the whole building and greater
apartment residents' awareness of controlling their own consumption and continuing to
repair fixtures that resumed leaking. The current program would tentatively follow an
identical approach.
(a)   It is proposed that under the project USAG would purchase various parts
and fixtures needed to replace defective plumbing parts. These purchases
would be carried out over a three-year period according to needs and to
progress of the replacement campaign;
(b)   USAG would pass on the equipment to OSNAAK and the kantors and
charge them for the equipment cost on terms and conditions to be defined
over the next two months by the two organizations;
(c)   The kantors and OSNAAK  would in turn carry out the fixture
replacement. To provide reliable estimates of equipment needs and to
sensitize apartment residents, a preliminary investigation will be launched
by kantor staff over the next two months. This survey would help clarify
the modalities under which the carnpaign should be carried out, in
particular (i) the time when it should follow the metering campaign; and
(ii) the need to tackle all repairs within one building at a time; and the
terms of repayment for the equipment from the residents to the kantors (a
period of about one to two years with a down payment of, say, 20 percent
of the equipment cost would seem appropriate goals). The review of the
proposed modalities will be discussed in April with the IDA appraisal
mission and OSNAAK and kantors, and results of the surveys should be
available to the Project Office before then.
PILOT EXPERIENCE OF INDIVIDUAL METERING
13.   At the request of the Municipality and USAG, the project would include a pilot
program aiming at individual metering of apartment premises to be carried out in one or
two buildings during the second half of the project. The program would examine the
increased benefits of single apartment metering versus bloc building metering, in
particular the gain in water consumption monitoring and improvements realized in the
management and billing.

- 71-                      ANNEXSB
ANNEX 5B: USAG: CURRENT ORGANIZATION AND
DEVELOPMENT ACTION PLAN
Legal Status
14.   USAG, Ulaanbaatar's state-owned water and wastewater entity, has not been
registered under the 1995 Company Law, as it should have been, because of (a) lack of
the governing and auditing bodies required by the Company Law, and (b) Articles of
Association not in accordance with the Law. New draft Articles have been prepared and
will be revised to reflect the 1995 Company Law before they are approved by the
Municipality and duly registered. USAG's subscribed and unpaid capital have not been
properly estimated and updated due to the lack of assets revaluation. With completion of
these requirements, USAG's new legal status would give it more autonomy, although its
tariff structure and levels would remain under the Municipality's control. On attaining
company status, a performance contract should be finalized between the Municipality and
USAG to regulate municipal obligations regarding the tariff level and provide USAG
with required performance indicators.
Organizational Structure
15.   USAG's organizational structure has a horizontal configuration indicating that the
General Manager is responsible for most decision-making. Its organizational chart also
combines two bodies: USAG as well as the previously existing TANK Company, which
was incorporated into USAG but retained the organizational structure developed before
the incorporation. Furthermore, USAG's water- and sewer-related activities are not
separated in its operational divisions; for example, the Maintenance Division deals with
both the water and sewerage network. With such a structure, USAG cannot distinguish
its water and wastewater costs and therefore lacks adequate management information on
the performance of each part of the system. USAG also needs to arrange for establishing
the governing and auditing bodies required by the Company Law.
Operations and Maintenance
16.   USAG operates a water supply system that currently includes 300 km of water
pipelines and well fields of some 1 10 wells and pump stations, while the sewerage system
has an 80-km network that feeds into a wastewater treatment plant before discharge. In
addition, USAG/TANK provides water supply for the ger areas through 262 public water
kiosks, transporting water to the kiosks by water tanker trucks. Maintenance of all its
assets is very poor, comprising renovations, repairs and facility replacement carried out
only when absolutely necessary and often on an emergency basis. There are no specific
maintenance procedures, and many devices in the system do not work. The maintenance
budget is woefully insufficient.



-72 -                      ANNEX 5B
Financial and Accounting Statements
17.   The existing accounting system does not comply with international standards.
The system does not reflect costs related to each cost-generating center, and it is
impossible to determine whether or not the costs are reflected in water and wastewater
charges. Financial management is essentially limited to very basic budgeting without any
financial analysis. An asset revaluation system is virtually nonexistent.
Staffing
18.   USAG employs 1,074 people (including 442 in TANK). Considering the scope of
services provided by USAG, the company appears overstaffed. The typical efficiency
indicator for water supply and sewerage companies-i.e., the number of employees per
km of network operated-is very high for USAG: 632 persons for 380 km or 1.66
persons per km compared to a common standard of 0.45 staff per km. The wastewater
treatment plant, with 128 personnel, seems particularly overstaffed. USAG's managers
have technical, rather than financial and economics, training; only four managers have
university degrees in economics and no lawyer is on the staff.  Throughout the
organization, older staff predominate. Training is needed in all positions, especially in
advanced management techniques and up-to-date financial and accounting practices and
procedures for senior managers.
INSTITUTIONAL STRENGTHENING GOALS
19.   The main objective of USAG's institutional strengthening is to create an
enterprise capable of assuming greater autonomy in its operations and management, and
operating in a commercially-oriented environment.
20.   USAG's strengthening would be based on an institutional study prepared with
assistance from Australian consulting engineers, Sinclair Knight Merz, in July 1996. The
findings of the study, which included recommendations for USAG's reorganization and
improvement, were discussed with USAG's management during April 1997, and an
institutional action plan, incorporating modifications suggested by USAG, was confirmed
at that time.
USAG's DEVELOPMENT ACTION PLAN
21.   Regularization of Legal Status. The IDA Appraisal mission reviewed USAG's
existing Articles of Association and found them too general and not consistent with the
Upper Law. These Articles need further amendments to clarify: (a) the role of the Owner
and the Governing Board; (b) the legal responsibility, whether a limited liability company
or an State-owned enterprise; (c) procedure for establishing the Governing Board and
selecting its members, as well as its duties, powers and responsibilities; (d) procedures
and responsibility for tariff setting; and (e) USAG's authority to borrow funds from
domestic and international sources. The Municipality and USAG have agreed to revise
USAG's Articles prepared early May 1997 and to provide them to the Bank for further



- 73 -                     ANNEX5B
review and comment. Subsequently, after submission of the completed Application Form
approved by the State Property Agency, the Articles will be formally registered in the
State Register. Formal registration is expected to be completed by July 1, 1997. With
this, USAG will become a company with autonomy given through incorporation of its
Articles according to requirements of the Company Law.
22.   Organizational Restructuring. USAG's structure needs reorganization for two
main reasons:
*  The current outdated, inefficient organizational structure prevents efficient
operations and satisfactory financial and technical performance;
*  During and after implementation of the proposed project, new needs for water
services will arise, requiring additional capabilities in USAG.
* Within this context, USAG's internal reorganization would be implemented
gradually, in keeping with progress of the project's physical execution. The
following phased program for USAG's internal reorganization is
recommended.
Phase I: Separation of Water Supply and Wastewater Activities and Integration of the
TANK Company into USA G's Structure
23.   To distinguish water and wastewater expenditures in order to identify specific
costs and estimate appropriate water and sewer tariffs, the following change is
recommended:
* Transfer of sewer maintenance responsibility and activities without staff
transfer from USAG's Maintenance Department to a newly established
subdivision for this purpose in the Wastewater Treatment Plant.
24.   To integrate the TANK  company into USAG, the following steps are
recommended:
*  Incorporation of TANK staff for accounting, finance and personnel into
appropriate USAG divisions.
*  Incorporation of the kiosk maintenance division into USAG's new Building
Department dealing with all building structures.
*  Assumption  by USAG's existing Customer Services Department of
responsibility for collecting charges for ger area services formerly provided by
TANK and incorporation of kiosk operators into this Department.
25.   Phase I should begin immediately and be completed during the first six months of
project implementation.



- 74-                      ANNEX 5B
Phase 11: Reorganization during Implementation of the Project's Physical Investment
Program
26.   Implementation of the project's ger area water supply program and installation of
water meters in apartment blockhouses will create a need for additional services from
USAG. The new ger area water supply network will require maintenance, and the meters
installed in the apartment blockhouses as well as those in institutions, industry, CTPs will
require special maintenance services. The following changes for these purposes are
proposed:
*  Establishment of a Metering Department responsible for meter installation,
maintenance, replacement and calibration.
*  Strengthening of the Customer Services Department to handle meter reading,
billing, and collection, provision of demand forecasts for water supply
planning, dealing with customers' requests and complaints, and maintaining a
customer register by duureg, khoroo and plot. The project would provide
appropriate computer hardware, software and training for these purposes.
* Expansion of the Water Maintenance Department with operators responsible
for ger area water pipelines maintenance.
27.   This phase should begin during the second year of project implementation, in
combination with the physical installation of meters.
Phase III: AdditionalActivities
28.   USAG, as the company responsible for the municipal water and wastewater
system, should be responsible for all types of water-related activities. Therefore, it is
recommended that planning of water supply and sewerage investments as well as
supervision of investment implementation be transferred from the Municipality to USAG.
This would entail, in order of priority:.
.  Expansion of USAG's Technical Department with staff responsible for
mapping, establishment of quality standards, and assets evidence.
*  In the future, USAG may also need to establish additional departments
responsible for planning and execution of investments, preparation of small
construction works and some designs
This phase could be undertaken during or after project completion.
29.   With continued privatization of the Mongolian economy, privatization of the
water kiosks is may be envisioned. In this case, all kiosks and their operators would be
excluded from  USAG and become USAG's customers.  In addition, tank truck
privatization by leasing trucks to drivers would enable USAG to operate more efficiently,



- 75 -                      ANNEX5B
with fewer employees and equipment. USAG could then focus on its true business sector
activities.
Human Resources Management and Staff Allocation
30.   To address the human resource management and development issues related to
USAG's reorganization and overstaffing, the following actions are recommended:

31.   Attrition: A Solution to Overstaffing. USAG should address its overstaffing
problem by implementing a gradual, steady staff reduction program based on the
following assumptions:
* No extension of employment for those eligible for retirement.
* Release of workers not meeting performance standards for their positions.
* Release of staff not wishing to participate in the reorganization.
32.   During project appraisal USAG management agreed that staff would be reduced
in number from 1,074 presently to 956 by the end of project execution, and that further



-76-                      ANNEX5B
reductions would be considered. Currently hiring of new staff in proceeding to match
those going into retirement (54). Between now and 1999 retirees would not be replaced
by new recruiters, and staff employed could drop to 961 without any other release. A
tentative new organizational chart of USAG with the forecast number of staff by 2001 is
attached to this annex.
33.   Training of Personnel Department Staff. The Personnel Department should
undertake the following training, with one staff member made responsible for planning,
arranging and coordinating the training.
* Developing advanced techniques of human resources management geared to
staff selection for all positions based on a comparison of candidates'
qualifications and experience.
* Develop a public relations capability within USAG.
34.   Timing. Preparation of a detailed training program should begin immediately and
be completed by October 1, 1997. Thereafter, training would be provided in tandem with
the reorganization program.
Maintenance Development
35.   The maintenance budget should be increased over the 1996 budget in real terms
by 10 percent annually during the next five years. Thereafter, it should be maintained at a
level equivalent to the assets depreciation value. The maintenance fund to be established
would finance necessary equipment (e.g., pipe locators, plugs for closing off sewers,
sewer cleaning equipment, and meter calibration equipment). The proposed project
would finance technical assistance in maintenance and for development of a
comprehensive asset management program.
36.   Maintenance Department staff would receive training in the following areas:
*  Operation of water leakage detection equipment: 2 workers
*  Operation, installation, calibration and maintenance of water meters:  8
workers
*  Preparation of manuals giving detailed procedures for carrying out all
operations: 5 workers
*  Preparation of a comprehensive asset register for use in developing a routine
maintenance program: 2 persons
Financial and Accounting Development
37.  It is recommended that development of USAG's financial and accounting
capabilities cover the following activities:



- 77 -                    ANNEX SB
(a)   Separation of Water and Sewerage Costs. It is recommended that water
and sewerage operations be separated as soon as possible, and by
January 1, 1999, separate accounts should be kept for each operation in
order to identify the related costs and set the respective tariffs to cover
operating costs.  However, the costs of support and administration
departments, which do not belong to either water or sewerage, should be
handled by an internal system of charging the operating divisions in
proportion to their staff numbers.
(b)   Introduction of International Accounting System. Introduction of a
new accounting system in compliance with international accounting
standards should be completed by January 1, 1999. The accounting
system would allow a determination of real output and input costs related
to each unit. The proposed project would lay the basis for introducing the
new system by covering the cost of procuring appropriate computer
hardware and software and training 10 accounting staff.
(c)   Establishment of Financial Management System. Technical assistance
and training would be provided early in the project for developing a
comprehensive financial management system, including financial analysis
and projections, annual budgeting and control of income and expenditures.
38.  Introduction of Management Information System (MIS). An MIS system
should be developed for use at the highest management level, i.e., USAG's General
Manager and his deputies.
39.   USAG institutional operations would be monitored through the use of appropriate
reporting procedures. Under the above Technical Assistance programs, detailed reporting
procedures will be discussed with USAG and establish after its approval.
40.   The following approach is recommended for implementation: Departments and
subordinated divisions to the senior managers (Chief Engineer, Chief of Finance and
Administration, Chief of Supporting Activities) should be required to submit monthly
reports on their activities and responsibilities. The senior managers would synthesize
those reports and submit summaries to the General Director. Those summary reports, in
turn, should be reviewed, analyzed, and the General Director would prepare one final
report for submission to the Governing Board once a month. The Governing Board
should submit a revised report to the Auditor afterwards. The annual report prepared by
the General Director, approved by the Governing Board and reviewed by the Auditor,
would be presented to the Company Owner, the UB Municipality.
41.   The following monthly reports shall be submitted to the Chief Engineer, which is
responsible for maintenance:
(a)   Water Production Report prepared by the Production Department
including:

* water production (based on pumping hours and after CTP meters
installation - based on water measurements);
* energy consumption;
* indicator ratio: water production per energy consumption; and

Department including:

of pipe material and location;
* specification of other damages and their duration from notification to
the completion of repair;

Wastewater Department including:

pipe material and location;
* statement of repaired or replaced manholes, chambers and sewer pipes;
and
* specification of other damages and their duration from notification to
completion of repair.
(d)   Wastewater Treatment Monthly Report prepared by the Wastewater
Department subdivision including:
* record of sewage inflow quantity and quality;
* record of sewage outflow quantity and quality related to standards;
* record of BOD5 load reduction;
* energy consumption;
* indicator ratio: capacity of treated sewage per energy consumption;
and

October 15. The most significant are the following:
* water consumption plan; and
* financial plan including budgeting and financial projections
maintenance plan.

ANNEX 6: TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE TERMS OF
REFERENCE
A. INSTITUTIONAL DEVELOPMENT OF USAG-TERMS OF REFERENCE
Background
1.    The Government of Mongolia has applied to the International Development
Association (IDA) for a Credit amounting to $16.1 million, which is to be onlent to the
Water and Sewerage Management Company in Ulaanbaatar (USAG) to support its piped
connection of water supply to the Ger area kiosks and to improve the efficiency of its
water distribution network and tariff charging system. USAG intends to apply part of
these proceeds to develop its institutional capacity, particularly in the area of financial
and accounting system, management information system (MIS), asset management
program, billing and collection procedures, and technical training required to enhance the
skills of staff to meet the new demands envisaged in Institutional Development Action
Program. Special Technical Assistance (TA) is to be provided under this IDA Project to
help USAG to achieve these purposes.
2.    Despite its incorporation under 1991 Company Law, USAG has been working as
an operating arm of the municipality for daily operation and maintenance of water and
sewerage, lacking incentives as well as adequate organizational structures and authorities
as an efficient public utility. Under the Project, however, it is to be formally reorganized
under the 1995 Company Law with an adequate structure and authorities to ensure more
financial and operational autonomy to provide incentives for improving efficiency and to
define clear accountability. A detailed time-bound action program of institutional change
was agreed and to be implemented. To enhance the efficiency of the USAG through
institutional restructuring, however, MIS supported by a proper accounting and financial
management system needs to be put in place.
3.    Despite a recent government decree to require companies to adopt IAS principles,
USAG has yet to convert its old system to a new one consistent with IAS. Expected
change in billing and collection system and the separation of accounts between water
supply and sewerage operation also calls for corresponding changes. Newly added
unction of planning, budgeting, and design will also require a proper management
information system. In addition, development of a comprehensive system to define,
measure and monitor performances of various units and levels of management is a
prerequisite to an efficient organization. The TA will support the development of an
adequate MIS supported by financial and accounting software and procedures consistent
with IAS and new organizational mandate to improve efficiency of USAG.'



- 84 -                    ANNEX6
4.    Although a detailed action program for institutional development focusing on
streamlining organizational structure and redeployment of staff was agreed to be phased
into during the project implementation, a strong technical training program to arm
USAG's staff with required skills and expertise is essential to gamer the efficiency of the
USAG. Moreover, the agreed action program as well as identified training program also
would require some adjustments to meet the demands of changing circumstances as well
as to coordinate with the new MIS system. This would require a component of TA,
specifically addressing training and other supports for organizational change.
Objectives
5.    The objective of the TA is to enhance the efficiency of USAG by providing
USAG with a MIS backed up by computerized financial management and accounting
system that will enable planning, budgeting, control and performance monitoring, and
with technical training to improve technical competence of staff to help ensure the
smooth implementation of Action Program of Institutional Development. As such, the
TA will:
(a)   Develop/purchase and install computerized MIS backed up be a modem
financial, accounting and information systems and procedures in the
USAG; and
(b)   Train various levels of USAG's management and staff in the use of the
designed systems and procedures as well as other technical training
identified in the Action Program of Institutional Development.
Scope of Works
6.    Detailed scope of works are as follows:
(a)   Review the Institutional Development and Financial Aspects reports by
Sinclair Knight Merz and Staff Appraisal Report by IDA and other
relevant background reports;
(b)   Design and implement conversion to the new accounting system with
supporting rules and procedures to be consistent with IAS: This will
involve the establishment of basic ledger subsystem that includes, but is
not limited to, general ledger, accounts receivable, inventory, salaries, and
fixed assets, as well as setting up of cost centers and the cost accounting
system that enables separation of the cost between water supply and
sewerage operation;
(c)   Review the existing computer hardware and software and based on the
identified system requirement, help procure and install the required
hardware and software;



- 85 -                    ANNEX6
(d)   Review  and refine the current reporting system, define required
management and financial reports, particularly in view of the budgeting
and planning function, and help develop/purchase a financial management
system to generate required financial data and reports and five-year
financial projections supported by computerized software as appropriate;
(e)   Integrate the billing and collection subsystem to be developed by meter
installation company into the USAG's general MIS;
(f)   Integrate the maintenance program to be developed under a separate TA
into the USAG's general MIS;
(g)   Develop a comprehensive performance indicators to be used to measure
the performance of various units and level of management as well as
USAG as a whole and recommend the five-year targets reflecting the
current and planned institutional capacities;
(h)   Transfer the expertise in utilizing management information system,
accounting and financial software as well as accompanies procedures and
practices through on-the-job training and other venues based on the
detailed technology transfer program;
(i)   Review and adjust, if warranted, the Action Program for Institutional
Development and support the phase-in of Action Program; and
(j)    Review the training program identified under the Action Program for
Institutional Development and help carry out the agreed training program;
Timing and Budget
7.    The TA will require the services of a team of consultants with expertise in
financial management, accounting, MIS, and institutional development and organization
of training. A total of 16 person-months of international consultant input and 13 person-
months of domestic consultant services will expected. Total budget is estimated to be
$500,000 including contingencies. It is expected that the whole training program and
implementation assistance will start in January 1998 and will be finished in December
1999. The program will be carried out in phases as agreed with USAG.
8.    The IDA Credit includes funds for the purchase of equipment (e.g., computer
hardware and software) necessary for the implementation of financial management and
MIS. The equipment will be purchased by the consultant on behalf on USAG, and in
accordance with the IDA's procurement guidelines. The equipment will be left with
USAG upon the completion of the program.



- 86 -                     ANNEX6
B. PROJECT IMPLEMENTATION AND MANAGEMENT CONSULTANTs-TERMS OF
REFERENCE
Introduction
9.    Water Distribution System. The Municipality of Ulaanbaatar (MUB), Outer
Mongolia is about to commence implementation of an IDA-assisted Urban Services
Project, which includes improvements to Ulaanbaatar city's urban water distribution
system, a major change in the system for supplying water to 12 ger areas (population
169,400), from truck tanker supply to water-dispensing kiosks, to piped supply to
existing (280) and additional kiosks and the development of a ring main and reservoir
system to increase system reliability and efficiency and reduce excessive costs of
maintaining pressure by pumping.
10.   Ger areas are largely unserviced housing areas on the fringes of the city, housing
about 50 percent of UB's population in a mixture of traditional Mongolian tents (the ger),
wooden frame and some masonry structures.
11.   Ger Upgrading.  In addition, the project would provide for upgrading
infrastructure in five of the ger areas that would be obtaining piped water supply. The
infrastructure would include roads and paths, stormwater drainage and bathhouses and
washing facilities. The roads and path in particular have been selected to improve access
water kiosks by ger residents. The stormwater drainage projects aim at alleviating
flooding, erosion and loss of lives and property in the worst-affected ger areas in UB.
12.   Metering. All of UB's residential premises, particularly formal housing in
publicly-owned apartment buildings, and many institutional and industrial premises have
no water meters. Consumers have mainly been charged on the basis of per capita and
other "norms," instead of the quantity of water consumed, with the result that USAG is
earning revenue on less than 50 percent of its bulk water production and water wastage is
very high. A key component of the project would provide for the procurement and
installation, over the first three years of the project, of about 14,000 hot and cold water
meters in about 2,620 apartment blocks (not individual apartment units) and currently
unmetered institutional premises.
13.   Fixture Repairs and Replacements. Also, to assist residential consumers to
reduce water wastage, particularly when they are charged under the project on a
volumetric rather than normative basis, the project would fund an apartment fixture (taps
and toilets) repair and replacement program. USAG would bear the costs of the fixtures
and existing MUB housing management and maintenance organizations-the kantors-
would repair and install the fixtures.
14.   Modest provisions for rehabilitating critical elements of the wastewater collection,
treatment and disposal system are also included in the project.



- 87 -                    ANNEX6
Organizational Arrangements for Project Implementation.
15.   The water supply component of the Project would be implemented by the Water
Facilities Exploitation Department Of Ulaanbaatar City (USAG), a wholly MUB-owned
service operations and maintenance department, which is being converted legally,
institutionally and technically into a commercially-oriented Municipal Company owned
by MUB. The ger infrastructure upgrading component would be implemented by MUB's
Department of Architecture, Planning and Building and MUB Districts (Duuregs) and
subdistricts (Khoroos). With the assistance of international consultants, the project has
been prepared by a Project Preparation Group, headed by a Project Director from MUB's
Department of Architecture and Building and composed of staff from various MUB
Departments-including MUB's Departments of Construction, Architecture and Building
and Finance and Planning-the Ministry of Infrastructure Development and USAG. For
project implementation and management, MUB would establish and maintain a Project
Management Unit (PMU), composed of people deputized from the same agencies that
prepared and staffed the Project Preparation Group. The PMU would be responsible to
the MUB Deputy City Manager, through the Chief of the Department of Strategic Policy
and Planning, which has been assigned direct responsibility for overall Project
implementation.
16.   Local consultants would be separately recruited and employed to assist the PMU
in project management and implementation. These local consultants would work with the
international consultants from whom MUB seeks assistance under these Terms of
Reference and who would work with the PMU.
17.  International and local consultants will also be recruited under the project (with
separate Terms of Reference) to provide technical assistance to USAG for institutional
development, training, financial management, and development of programs for
maintenance improvements. In addition, the project would finance (under provisions
separate from this Terms of Reference) development of and training in the
computerization of USAG's billing and collection system for metered supplies.
18.   MUB wish to appoint a suitably qualified international firm to act as Project
Implementation and Management Consultant ("the Consultant") to assist the PMU and
the implementing agencies with implementation management.
19.  In view of the substantial number of contracts to be let under the Project, the need
to prepare designs and bid documents for the second through fifth years of the project,
and MUB's very limited experience in managing an IDA-financed project, MUB wishes
to develop standardized procedures for the review of detailed designs, specifications and
bills of quantities, the prequalification of contractors, preparation of contract
documentation, the evaluation and award of contracts and to establish an appropriate
system to manage and monitor project implementation.



- 88 -                     ANNEX6
Scope of Work
20.   The Consultant will assist MUB to:
(a)   review detailed designs and technical specifications, where necessary, for
all project components;
(b)   prepare ICB and NCB bid documents, satisfactory to MUB and IDA on
the basis of the model documents prepared for first-year projects during
project preparation;
(c)   prequalify and postqualify bidders and identify potential suppliers;
(d)   establish standard tendering and bid evaluation procedures to conform to
IDA procurement guidelines and principles;
(e)   establish contract implementation, procurement and engineering quality
control criteria and procedures for monitoring; and
(f)   implement a construction and equipment installation management system
for civil works and equipment-particularly with regard to the meter
installation and fixture repair and replacement programs.
21.   Bid Documents. During finalization of bid documents, the Consultant will
review engineering designs, specifications and other relevant documentation to ensure
that they conform to good design practice and to IDA guidelines and particularly that cold
climate technical requirements are being adequately met. Bid documents will be subject
to review by IDA.
22.   Review of Technical Specifications.  Standard technical specifications are
available for many items, but there will be cases where modifications or additions may be
appropriate. Where necessary, the consultant will assist MUB to draft revisions or
additions for inclusion in the relevant bid documents.
23.   Pre- and  Postqualification.   Where contractor prequalification  and/or
postqualification is required, the Consultant will assist MUB to advertise for potential
contractors to prequalify, to evaluate prequalification and postqualification submissions
and to establish shortlists for bidding.
24.   Tendering and Bid Evaluation. The Consultant will assist MUB to establish
and administer standard procedures for competitive bidding and award in accordance with
IDA Guidelines and project agreements in relation to International and National
Competitive Bidding (ICB and NCB) and for International and National Shopping. The
Consultant will advise on relevant international and local suppliers where appropriate.
25.   Quality Control. MUB and IDA wish to ensure that civil works and equipment
installations implemented under the Project are of a high standard and will therefore



- 89 -                     ANNEX6
require guidance from the Consultant in establishing appropriate quality monitoring and
reporting procedures.
26.   Construction Management System. The Consultant will assist the Municipality
to establish an information system to manage contracts and monitor implementation
progress, including monitoring expenditure and time required for contract(s)
implementation, payments to contractors and applications for withdrawal of IDA funds.
The system should be designed to identify problems at an early stage and to provide
project progress information for the MUB and the IDA at regular intervals.
27.   Institutional. The Consultant will assist MUB to prepare periodic progress
reports for Government and IDA, consolidating the progress on project components
implemented by MUB and USAG. The consultant will also assist MUB to monitor
compliance with the Credit Covenants, Project Action Plans, provisions for audits and
accounts, and financial and other project performance targets.
28.   In-City Training Seminars. The Consultant will conduct at least one in-city
training seminar in the city during the period of the consultancy contract. These seminars
would be expected to extend over a period of about 15 days and would be attended by
selected personnel from the city. The seminars would address topics of relevance to the
city, including specification and design, prequalification, bidding, evaluation and award
of contracts, contract management and supervision, quality control, saLety procedures,
operations and maintenance. Additionally, the Consultant would address topics of
specific relevance such as cold climate utilities design and construction.
Consultant Team
29.   The consultant will be expected to provide intermittent technical assistance to
MUB over a period of two to three years commencing, if possible, late 1997. During the
initial stages, frequent advice is likely to be needed. Subsequently, once standard
procedures and working methods have been established, the need for technical advice and
the frequency of visits will reduce.
30.  In view of the need for frequent, short visits, the Consultant may wish to work
from a regional office within Mongolia or China, which is near Outer Mongolia. In any
event, the Consultant should arrange good communication facilities between their office,
the Municipality and IDA in Washington.
31.   The Consultant will provide about 32 person-months of professional staff input,
approximately 18 months in year 1, 10 months in years 2, and 4 months in year 3, and
will appoint a Senior Project Management Advisor/Team Leader as prime representative
(table annexed). The Team Leader will be a senior Municipal services engineer, with
substantial water and sewerage experience, having appropriate regional experience and
familiarity with IDA procedures and procurement guidelines.



-90 -                      ANNEX6
32.   The Consultant will be fully responsible for the provision of the necessary skills
within the teamn. The Consultant's staff will be expected to be appropriately qualified and
to have experience in Mongolia or elsewhere in the region in the following technical
fields:
(a)   IDA procurement procedures for civil works and equipment;
(b)   contract management and supervision;
(c)   quality control for civil works; and
(d)   municipal  engineering,  including  the  design,  construction  and
management of water supply and distribution pipelines, pumping stations
and systems, the design, operation, management and monitoring of sewage
treatment plants and the design and construction of roads and storm
drainage systems.
Schedule and Reporting
33.   The technical assistance to be provided under these Terms of Reference will
commence as soon as possible and will continue for a period of two to three years.
34.   The Consultant will submit brief, monthly reports during the first full year of the
contract and quarterly reports during subsequent years summarizing progress achieved,
difficulties encountered and issues to be resolved.  Six copies of each report (in
Mongolian) will be sent to MUB and three copies (in English) to IDA in Washington.
Where the Consultant assists materially in the modification or preparation of designs,
specifications or other relevant documents, the Consultant will send three copies to IDA,
for information only.
Materials, Data and Support Services
35.   The Consultant, when providing technical assistance, will work in the offices of
MUB who will provide appropriately furnished office accommodation at no cost to the
Consultant. All available data, and mapping will be provided at no cost to the
Consultant.
36.   The costs of computers and related office equipment and software, vehicles and
office support and interpreters should be included in consultants' proposals and are
estimated in the table attached. These costs would be in addition to the computers and
related office equipment and software and vehicles that are already available in the
Project office and that would be made available by MUB to the consultants from whom
assistance is being sought under these Terms of Reference.
37.   MUB will provide appropriate counterpart and support staff to work with the
Consultant, and will arrange introductions to other agencies as required.



-91-                       ANNEX6
38.   The Consultant will bear all payroll costs of its staff, plus all costs incurred by its
staff in connection with international travel, accommodation and subsistence.
39.   The Consultant will be reimbursed, at cost, for any expenses reasonably incurred
in connection with telecommunications, courier services and printing, and local travel
related to the provision of these consultancy services.
